**Result:**

     1→# Code Correctness Report: types-and-lib  
     2→  
     3→**Agent:** epcp-code-correctness-agent  
     4→**Domain:** types-and-lib  
     5→**Files audited:** 10  
     6→**Date:** 2026-02-17T00:18:00Z  
     7→  
     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    10→### [CC-001] `params` type mismatch in agent transfer route (non-Promise in Next.js 14.2)  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts:33  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. Every other `[id]` route in this codebase (40+ occurrences) uses `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }` with `const { id } = await params`. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // Line 31-37 of transfer/route.ts  
    19→  export async function POST(  
    20→    request: Request,  
    21→    { params }: { params: { id: string } }  // <-- non-Promise  
    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.  
    36→  
    37→### [CC-002] Transfer approval creates inconsistent state when destination team i  

... [12794 more chars truncated]

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/[taskId]/route.ts:93-114  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** logic  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The DELETE handler does not wrap its body in a try/catch block. If `await params`, `getTeam()`, `checkTeamAccess()`, or `deleteTask()` throw an unexpected exception, Next.js will return an opaque 500 error with no JSON body. The PUT handler in the same file has a try/catch, so this is an inconsistency within the same route file.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```typescript  
    22→// Line 93-114: No try/catch  
    23→export async function DELETE(  
    24→  request: NextRequest,  
    25→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; taskId: string }> }  
    26→) {  
    27→  const { id, taskId } = await params  
    28→  const team = getTeam(id)  
    29→  // ... no error boundary ...  
    30→  const deleted = deleteTask(id, taskId)  
    31→  if (!deleted) {  
    32→    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Task not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    33→  }  
    34→  return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    35→}  
    36→```  
    37→- **Fix:** Wrap the DELETE handler body in a try/catch with a `console.error` and a 500 JSON response, matching the pattern used in the PUT handler.  
    38→  
    39→### [CC-002] Missing try/catch in GET /api/teams/[id]/tasks

    14→### [CC-001] Race condition: stale `refresh()` response when `agentId` changes rapidly  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.ts:63-100  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. If `agentId` changes while fetches are in-flight (e.g., user clicks between agents quickly), the older fetch's `.then()` handler will overwrite state with data that no longer matches the current `agentId`. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // Line 63-100  
    23→  const refresh = useCallback(() => {  
    24→    setLoading(true)  
    25→    Promise.all([  
    26→      fetch('/api/governance').then(...)  // <-- no AbortController  
    27→      fetch('/api/teams').then(...)  
    28→      fetch('/api/governance/transfers?status=pending').then(...)  
    29→    ])  
    30→      .then(([govData, teamsData, transfersData]) => {  
    31→        // These run even if agentId changed since the fetch started  
    32→        setHasPassword(govData.hasPassword ?? false)  
    33→        setAllTeams(teamsData.teams ?? [])  
    34→        setPendingTransfers(transfersData.requests ?? [])  
    35→      })  
    36→      ...  
    37→  }, [agentId])  
    38→  ```

    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/scripts/remote-install.sh:1225  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** shell  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED (tested on macOS)  
    19→- **Description:** The `gw_list` variable is built with literal `\n` strings (shell does not expand `\n` in double-quoted string assignment). When `portable_sed` substitutes `{{ACTIVE_GATEWAYS_LIST}}` in MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md, the result is a single line containing `- Slack\n- Discord` literally, rather than separate lines with actual newlines. The template at `scripts/MAILMAN-CLAUDE.md:14` expects a multi-line bullet list.  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→```bash  
    22→# Line 1224-1225:  
    23→if [ -n "$gw_list" ]; then  
    24→    gw_list="${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"  
    25→```  
    26→On macOS, `"${gw_list}\n- ${gw_display}"` produces the literal string `- Slack\n- Discord`, not `- Slack` + newline + `- Discord`.  
    27→- **Fix:** Use `$'\n'` for actual newlines, or use `printf` to build the string:  
    28→```bash  
    29→gw_list="${gw_list}"$'\n'"- ${gw_display}"  
    30→```  
    31→Or alternatively use `printf '%s\n' "- ${gw_display}"` to append to the variable.

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:07:32]*

<details open>
<summary>🤖 Subagent (spark): Fix useTeam optimistic revert (HK-004,006)</summary>

**Input:**

**Agent:** `spark` | **Description:** Fix useTeam optimistic revert (HK-004,006)  

Fix 2 issues in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts  

ISSUE HK-004: updateTeam optimistic update doesn't revert on network error (thrown exception). Only reverts on HTTP error (!res.ok).  

FIX: Wrap the fetch+response handling in try/catch, calling fetchTeam() in catch to revert:  
```typescript
const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: Partial<Team>) => {
  if (!teamId) return
  setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
  try {
    const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`, {
      method: 'PUT',
      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
      body: JSON.stringify(updates),
    })
    if (!res.ok) {
      await fetchTeam()  // Revert optimistic update on HTTP error
      throw new Error('Failed to update team')
    }
    const data = await res.json()
    setTeam(data.team)
  } catch (err) {
    await fetchTeam()  // Revert optimistic update on network error too
    throw err
  }
}, [teamId, fetchTeam])
... [751 more chars]

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FFC107; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

NIT TL-005 was about using a stricter UUID pattern. The current regex `/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i` allows invalid UUIDs. Let me fix this and the remaining few NITs that the agents may not have covered.  

</div>


## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:37:08]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `task-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
  if (!/^[0-9a-f-]{36}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')
```

**New:**  
```
  // Strict UUID v4 pattern (8-4-4-4-12 hex groups) to prevent path traversal
  if (!/^[0-9a-f]{8}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{4}-[0-9a-f]{12}$/i.test(teamId)) throw new Error('Invalid team ID')
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:07:19]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `route.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/[taskId]/route.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
export async function DELETE(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; taskId: string }> }
) {
  const { id, taskId } = await params
  const team = getTeam(id)
  if (!team) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
  }
  const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
  const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
  if (!access.allowed) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
  }

  const deleted = await deleteTask(id, taskId)
  if (!deleted) {
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Task not found' }, { status: 404 })
  }

  return NextResponse.json({ success: true })
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function DELETE(
  request: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string; taskId: string }> }
) {
  try {
    const { id, taskId } = await params
    const team = getTeam(id)
    if (!team) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Team not found' }, { status: 404 })
    }
    const agentId = request.headers.get('X-Agent-Id') || undefined
    const access = checkTeamAccess({ teamId: id, requestingAgentId: agentId })
    if (!access.allowed) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: access.reason }, { status: 403 })
    }

    const deleted = await deleteTask(id, taskId)
    if (!deleted) {
      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Task not found' }, { status: 404 })
    }

    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error deleting task:', error)
    return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Internal server error' }, { status: 500 })
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/teams/[id]/tasks/[taskId]/route.ts has been updated successfully.

     1→#!/bin/bash  
     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0  
     9→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh 0.18.0   # Set specific version  
    10→  
    11→set -e  
    12→  
    13→# Colors  
    14→RED='\033[0;31m'  
    15→GREEN='\033[0;32m'  
    16→YELLOW='\033[1;33m'  
    17→CYAN='\033[0;36m'  
    18→NC='\033[0m'  
    19→  
    20→# Get script directory and project root  
    21→SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"  
    22→PROJECT_ROOT="$(dirname "$SCRIPT_DIR")"  
    23→  
    24→# Read current version from version.json  
    25→VERSION_FILE="$PROJECT_ROOT/version.json"  
    26→if [ ! -f "$VERSION_FILE" ]; then  
    27→    echo -e "${RED}Error: version.json not found${NC}"  
    28→    exit 1  
    29→fi  
    30→  
    31→CURRENT_VERSION=$(grep -o '"version": *"[^"]*"' "$VERSION_FILE" | cut -d'"' -f4)  
    32→echo -e "${CYAN}Current version: ${CURRENT_VERSION}${NC}"  
    33→  
    34→# Parse current version  
    35→IFS='.' read -r MAJOR MINOR PATCH <<< "$CURRENT_VERSION"  
    36→  
    37→# Determine new version  
    38→case "$1" in  
    39→    patch)  
    40→        PATCH=$((PATCH + 1))  
    41→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    42→        ;;  
    43→    minor)  
    44→        MINOR=$((MINOR + 1))  
    45→        PATCH=0  
    46→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    47→        ;;  
    48→    major)  
    49→        MAJOR=$((MAJOR + 1))  
    50→        MINOR=0  
    51→        PATCH=0  
    52→        NEW_VERSION="${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}"  
    53→        ;;  
    54→    "")  
    55→        echo ""  
    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"  
    57→        echo ""  
    58→        echo "Examples:"  
    59→        echo "  $0 patch    # ${CURRENT_VERSION} -> ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.$((PATCH + 1

    63→}  
    64→  
    65→/** Verify plaintext against stored password hash. Returns false if no password set. */  
    66→export function verifyPassword(plaintext: string): boolean {  
    67→  const config = loadGovernance()  
    68→  if (!config.passwordHash) {  
    69→    // Constant-time defense: run bcrypt compare even when no password is set,  
    70→    // so the response time is identical whether or not a password hash exists.  
    71→    // This prevents a timing side-channel that would reveal password existence.  
    72→    bcrypt.compareSync(plaintext, '$2a$12$K4IuHqpKTnQUgPGRLFcIOuThtYEA/7HMp3Mt8hPoNYrxHhOscu3pS')  
    73→    return false  
    74→  }  
    75→  return bcrypt.compareSync(plaintext, config.passwordHash)  
    76→}  
    77→  
    78→/** Get the current manager agent ID, or null if none set */  
    79→export function getManagerId(): string | null {  
    80→  const config = loadGovernance()  
    81→  return config.managerId  
    82→}

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix 3 MUST-FIX issues in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/governance/transfers/[id]/resolve/route.ts  

AND fix 1 MUST-FIX in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts  

ISSUE 1 (AG-001 - agents transfer route): The params type is `{ params: { id: string } }` (non-Promise) and uses `params.id` synchronously. All other routes use `Promise<{ id: string }>` with `await params`. Also uses `Request` instead of `NextRequest`.  

FIX for agents transfer route:  
- Change `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` to `{ params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }`  
- Add `const { id } = await params` at top of function body  
- Replace all `params.id` with `id`  
- Change `Request` to `NextRequest` and add/verify import  

ISSUE 2 (AG-002 - governance resolve route): Transfer is marked as 'approved' BEFORE checking if destination team exists. If dest team is deleted, transfer is stuck as 'approved' but agent never moved.  

FIX: Move the destination team existence check BEFORE calling resolveTransferRequest(). The flow should be:  
1. Read teams inside lock (already done)  
2. Check destination team exists — if not, return 404 WITHOUT resolving the transfer  
3. THEN call resolveTransferRequest() to mark approved/rejected  
4. THEN mutate teams  

ISSUE 3 (AG-003 - governance resolve route): `saveTeams(teams)` return value is ignored. If write fails, transfer is marked approved but teams not updated.  

FIX: Check the return value: `if (!saveTeams(teams)) { return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Failed to save team changes' }, { status: 500 }) }`  

Read both files first, understand the current flow, then make minimal edits.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - brief result"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator

useEffect(() => {
  const controller = new AbortController()
  refresh(controller.signal)
  return () => controller.abort()
}, [agentId, refresh])

const refresh = useCallback((signal?: AbortSignal) => {
```

```typescript
.then(([govData, teamsData, transfersData]) => {

  // ... existing setters ...

ISSUE HK-005 (NIT): refresh() doesn't use agentId in body but has it in deps.  

FIX: Remove `agentId` from the refresh useCallback dependency array. Change `[agentId]` to `[]`. The useEffect already depends on agentId and calls refresh when it changes.  

ISSUE HK-002: addAgentToTeam/removeAgentFromTeam read-modify-write race.  

FIX: This is a server-side design issue. Add a comment above both functions documenting the limitation:  
```typescript
// Note: This uses a client-side read-modify-write pattern (GET team -> modify agentIds -> PUT).
// Concurrent calls can race. Server-side atomic add/remove operations would be the proper fix.
// For Phase 1, UI buttons are disabled during operations which mitigates the risk.
```

  const refresh = useCallback(() => {
    // Fetch governance state and teams in parallel
    setLoading(true)
    Promise.all([
      fetch('/api/governance').then((r) => {
        if (!r.ok) throw new Error('Request failed')
        return r.json()
      }).catch(() => ({ hasPassword: false, hasManager: false, managerId: null, managerName: null })),
      fetch('/api/teams').then((r) => {
        if (!r.ok) throw new Error('Request failed')
        return r.json()
      }).catch(() => ({ teams: [] })),
      fetch('/api/governance/transfers?status=pending').then((r) => {
        if (!r.ok) throw new Error('Request failed')
        return r.json()
      }).catch(() => ({ requests: [] })),
    ])
      .then(([govData, teamsData, transfersData]) => {
        setHasPassword(govData.hasPassword ?? false)
        setHasManager(govData.hasManager ?? false)
        setManagerId(govData.managerId ?? null)
        setManagerName(govData.managerName ?? null)
        setAllTeams(teamsData.teams ?? [])
        setPendingTransfers(transfersData.requests ?? [])
      })
      .catch(() => {
        // On fetch failure, reset to safe defaults
        setHasPassword(false)
        setHasManager(false)
        setManagerId(null)
        setManagerName(null)
        setAllTeams([])
        setPendingTransfers([])
      })
      .finally(() => {
        setLoading(false)
      })
  }, [agentId])
```

     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/transfer/route.ts:33  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** type-safety  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript

    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

     8→## MUST-FIX

    10→_None found._  
    11→  
    12→## SHOULD-FIX  
    13→  
    14→### [CC-001] Race condition: stale `refresh()` response when `agentId` changes rapidly  
    15→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useGovernance.ts:63-100  
    16→- **Severity:** SHOULD-FIX  
    17→- **Category:** race-condition  
    18→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. If `agentId` changes while fetches are in-flight (e.g., user clicks between agents quickly), the older fetch's `.then()` handler will overwrite state with data that no longer matches the current `agentId`. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).  
    20→- **Evidence:**  
    21→  ```typescript  
    22→  // Line 63-100  
    23→  const refresh = useCallback(() => {  
    24→    setLoading(true)

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:05:01]*

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team

    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}

    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

   126→  }  
   127→  
   128→  // Step 7: Default — allow  
   129→  return { allowed: true }  
   130→}

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }  
    39→}

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Send - Web UI message composition + routing  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Replaces the write half of sendMessage() / forwardMessage() from messageQueue.ts.  
     5→ * Web UI endpoints (/api/messages POST, /api/agents/[id]/messages POST, etc.) call  
     6→ * sendFromUI() and forwardFromUI().  
     7→ *  
     8→ * Flow:  
     9→ *   1. Resolve sender/recipient agents  
    10→ *   2. Build AMP envelope + payload  
    11→ *   3. Apply content security  
    12→ *   4. Local → deliver(), Remote → HTTP forward, External+offline → relay queue  
    13→ *   5. Write sender's sent folder  
    14→ *   6. Return Message object for response compatibility  
    15→ */

     8→## MUST-FIX  
     9→  
    10→### [CC-001] task-registry.ts: No file locking on write operations — race condition  
    11→- **File:** /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/task-registry.ts:95,132,179  
    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX  
    13→- **Category:** race-condition  
    14→- **Confidence:** CONFIRMED  
    15→- **Description:** `createTask()`, `updateTask()`, and `deleteTask()` all perform read-modify-write sequences (`loadTasks` -> mutate -> `saveTasks`) without any file locking. Unlike `team-registry.ts`, `transfer-registry.ts`, and `governance.ts`, which all use `withLock()` from `@/lib/file-lock`, `task-registry.ts` does not import or use `withLock` at all. Two concurrent API requests to create/update/delete tasks on the same team will race: both read the same file, mutate independently, and the second write silently overwrites the first, losing data.  
    16→- **Evidence:**  
    17→  ```typescript  
    18→  // lib/task-registry.ts — NO withLock anywhere in this file  
    19→  export function createTask(data: { teamId: string; ... }): Task {  
    20→    const tasks = loadTasks(data.teamId)  // READ  
    21→    // ... build task ...  
    22→    tasks.push(task)                       // MUTATE  
    23→    saveTasks(data.teamId, tasks)          // WRITE — can overwrite concurrent changes  
    24→    return task  
    25→  }  
    26→  ```  
    27→  Compare with `team-registry.ts` which wraps every write in `withLock('teams', () => { ... })`.  
    28→- **Fix:** Import `withLock` from `@/lib/file-lock` and wrap `createTask`, `updateTask`, and `deleteTask` in `withLock('tasks-' + teamId, ...)`. This requires making them `async` (matching the pattern in `team-registry.ts`). Note: `wouldCreateCycle` is read-only and does not need locking.  
    29→  
    30→## SHOULD-FIX  
    31→  

... [10731 more chars truncated]  

</details>

    12→- **Severity:** MUST-FIX

    15→- **Description:** The route handler uses `{ params }: { params: { id: string } }` and accesses `params.id` synchronously at line 37. This project runs Next.js 14.2.35 where params is a Promise in App Router route handlers. Synchronous access works today because Next.js resolves it internally, but it emits a deprecation warning and will break in Next.js 15.  
    16→- **Evidence:**

    22→  ) {  
    23→    try {  
    24→      let agent = getAgent(params.id)  // <-- synchronous access  
    25→  ```  
    26→  vs. all other routes:  
    27→  ```typescript  
    28→  // Example from resolve/route.ts line 14-19  
    29→  export async function POST(  
    30→    request: NextRequest,  
    31→    { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  // <-- Promise  
    32→  ) {  
    33→    const { id } = await params  // <-- awaited  
    34→  ```  
    35→- **Fix:** Change type to `Promise<{ id: string }>` and add `const { id } = await params` at the top of the function. Also change `Request` to `NextRequest` for consistency.

    19→- **Description:** The `refresh` callback fires three parallel fetches and unconditionally writes results to state. Because `refresh` is re-created via `useCallback([agentId])`, the old closure's `setLoading`/`setAllTeams`/etc. still reference the same state setters. There is no cancellation (AbortController) and no staleness guard (e.g., checking a ref against current agentId before calling setState).

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *  
     5→ * Open teams (type undefined or 'open') impose no restrictions.  
     6→ * Closed teams restrict access to the manager, chief-of-staff,  
     7→ * and team members only.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager } from './governance'  
    11→import { getTeam } from './team-registry'  
    12→  
    13→export interface TeamAccessInput {  
    14→  teamId: string  
    15→  requestingAgentId?: string // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface TeamAccessResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Determine whether the requester may access the team's resources.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.   

... [474 more chars truncated]  

</details>

     2→import { loadGovernance, setPassword, verifyPassword } from '@/lib/governance'  
     3→  
     4→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
     5→  try {  
     6→    const body = await request.json()  
     7→    const { password, currentPassword } = body  
     8→  
     9→    if (!password || typeof password !== 'string' || password.length < 6) {  
    10→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Password must be at least 6 characters' }, { status: 400 })  
    11→    }  
    12→  
    13→    const config = loadGovernance()  
    14→  
    15→    // If password already set, require current password  
    16→    if (config.passwordHash) {  
    17→      if (!currentPassword || !verifyPassword(currentPassword)) {  
    18→        return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Invalid current password' }, { status: 401 })  
    19→      }  
    20→    }  
    21→  
    22→    const isChange = !!config.passwordHash  
    23→    await setPassword(password)  
    24→  
    25→    if (isChange) {  
    26→      console.log('[governance] Password changed at', new Date().toISOString())  
    27→    } else {  
    28→      console.log('[governance] Password set at', new Date().toISOString())  
    29→    }  
    30→  
    31→    return NextResponse.json({ success: true })  
    32→  } catch (error) {  
    33→    console.error('Failed to set password:', error)  
    34→    return NextResponse.json(  
    35→      { error: error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Failed to set password' },  
    36→      { status: 500 }  
    37→    )  
    38→  }  
    39→}

```typescript
useEffect(() => {
  if (!isOpen) return
  const handleKey = (e: KeyboardEvent) => { if (e.key === 'Escape') handleClose() }
  document.addEventListener('keydown', handleKey)
  return () => document.removeEventListener('keydown', handleKey)
}, [isOpen])
```

ISSUE TL-003: If a COS is listed as chiefOfStaffId but NOT in agentIds (data corruption), they become invisible to the message filter because senderTeams uses agentIds.includes() only.  

FIX: In the COS-specific logic (step 4, around line 83), also derive COS teams from chiefOfStaffId, not just agentIds. Specifically:  

After the existing `senderTeams` definition (~line 52), add a `senderCosTeams` variable:  
```typescript
const senderCosTeams = closedTeams.filter(t => t.chiefOfStaffId === senderAgentId)
```

```typescript
// COS can reach members of teams they manage (even if not in agentIds due to data inconsistency)
const cosCanReach = [...senderTeams, ...senderCosTeams].some(team => 
  team.agentIds.includes(recipientAgentId) || team.chiefOfStaffId === recipientAgentId
)
```

Add a comment explaining this is a defensive check for data consistency.

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team

    25→ *

    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)

    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */

    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted

      <div className="flex flex-col h-screen bg-gray-950 text-white">
        <div className="flex-1 flex items-center justify-center">
          <div className="text-center">
            <div className="w-10 h-10 mx-auto mb-3 border-4 border-emerald-500 border-t-transparent rounded-full animate-spin" />
            <p className="text-sm text-gray-400">{loading ? 'Loading team...' : 'Team not found'}</p>
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
    )
  }
```

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation

    20→  reason?: string

    22→

    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm (R6.1–R6.7):  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior) (R6.4)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed (R6.3)  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members (R6.2)  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS (R6.1)  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied (R6.5)  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ *  
    35→ * IMPORTANT (R6.7): Uses getClosedTeamsForAgent (plural) to correctly handle  
    36→ * COS agents who belong to multiple closed teams simultaneously.  
    37→ */  
    38→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    39→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    40→  
    41→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    42→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    43→    return { allowed: true }  
    44→  }

    17→const TRANSFERS_FILE = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'governance-transfers.json')  
    18→  
    19→function ensureDir(): void {  
    20→  if (!existsSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR)) {  
    21→    mkdirSync(AIMAESTRO_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    22→  }  
    23→}  
    24→  
    25→/** Load all transfer requests from disk */  
    26→export function loadTransfers(): TransferRequest[] {  
    27→  ensureDir()  
    28→  if (!existsSync(TRANSFERS_FILE)) {  
    29→    return []  
    30→  }  
    31→  try {  
    32→    const raw = readFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    33→    const data: TransfersFile = JSON.parse(raw)  
    34→    return data.requests || []  
    35→  } catch {  
    36→    return []  
    37→  }  
    38→}  
    39→  
    40→/** Save transfer requests to disk */  
    41→function saveTransfers(requests: TransferRequest[]): void {  
    42→  ensureDir()  
    43→  const data: TransfersFile = { version: 1, requests }  
    44→  writeFileSync(TRANSFERS_FILE, JSON.stringify(data, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    45→}  
    46→

    55→  return

     2→ * Resolve (approve/reject) a transfer request  
     3→ * POST - Approve or reject a pending transfer

     7→import { getTransferRequest, resolveTransferRequest } from '@/lib/transfer-registry'  
     8→import { loadTeams, saveTeams, TeamValidationException } from '@/lib/team-registry'  
     9→import { isManager, getManagerId, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere } from '@/lib/governance'  
    10→import { getAgent } from '@/lib/agent-registry'  
    11→import { notifyAgent } from '@/lib/notification-service'  
    12→import { acquireLock } from '@/lib/file-lock'  
    13→  
    14→export async function POST(  
    15→  request: NextRequest,  
    16→  { params }: { params: Promise<{ id: string }> }  
    17→) {  
    18→  try {  
    19→    const { id } = await params  
    20→    const body = await request.json()  
    21→    const { action, resolvedBy, rejectReason } = body  
    22→  
    23→    if (!action || !resolvedBy) {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action and resolvedBy are required' }, { status: 400 })  
    25→    }  
    26→    if (action !== 'approve' && action !== 'reject') {  
    27→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'action must be "approve" or "reject"' }, { status: 400 })  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    // Get the transfer request  
    31→    const transferReq = getTransferRequest(id)  
    32→    if (!transferReq) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request not found' }, { status: 404 })  
    34→    }  
    35→    if (transferReq.status !== 'pending') {  
    36→      return NextResponse.json({ error: 'Transfer request is already resolved' }, { status: 409 })  
    37→    }  
    38→  
    39→    // Acquire teams lock for the entire read-validate-write cycle to prevent TOCTOU races.  
    40→    // We use acquireLock directly (instead of withLock) because we need to return  
    41→    // NextResponse objects from within the critical section.  
    42→    const releaseLock

     4→import type { Team } from '@/types/team'

     6→interface UseTeamResult {

    14→export function useTeam(teamId: string | null): UseTeamResult {  
    15→  const [team, setTeam] = useState<Team | null>(null)  
    16→  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)  
    17→  const [error, setError] = useState<string | null>(null)  
    18→  
    19→  const fetchTeam = useCallback(async () => {  
    20→    if (!teamId) return  
    21→    try {  
    22→      const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`)  
    23→      if (!res.ok) throw new Error('Failed to fetch team')  
    24→      const data = await res.json()  
    25→      setTeam(data.team || null)  
    26→      setError(null)  
    27→    } catch (err) {  
    28→      setError(err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Failed to fetch team')  
    29→    }  
    30→  }, [teamId])  
    31→  
    32→  // Initial fetch  
    33→  useEffect(() => {  
    34→    if (!teamId) {  
    35→      setTeam(null)  
    36→      setLoading(false)  
    37→      return  
    38→    }  
    39→    setLoading(true)  
    40→    fetchTeam().finally(() => setLoading(false))  
    41→  }, [teamId, fetchTeam])  
    42→  
    43→  const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: { name?: string; description?: string; agentIds?: string[]; instructions?: string }) => {  
    44→    if (!teamId) return  
    45→    // Optimistic update  
    46→    setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)  
    47→    const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`, {  
    48→      method: 'PUT',  
    49→      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },  
    50→      body: JSON.stringify({

     2→# AI Maestro - Version Bump Script  
     3→# Centralizes version management across all files  
     4→#  
     5→# Usage:  
     6→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh patch    # 0.17.12 -> 0.17.13  
     7→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh minor    # 0.17.12 -> 0.18.0  
     8→#   ./scripts/bump-version.sh major    # 0.17.12 -> 1.0.0

    53→        ;;

    56→        echo "Usage: $0 <patch|minor|major|version>"

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `file-lock.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/file-lock.ts"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * File Lock — in-process mutex for serializing load→modify→save operations  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Prevents concurrent read-modify-write races within a single Node.js process.  
     5→ * Each registry file gets its own named lock. When one API request is mid-write,  
     6→ * other requests for the same file queue up and run sequentially.  
     7→ *  
     8→ * This is sufficient for Phase 1 (single Next.js process, localhost).  
     9→ * For multi-process deployments, replace with advisory file locks (e.g., proper-lockfile).  
    10→ */  
    11→  
    12→// Map of lock name -> queue of pending resolve callbacks  
    13→const locks = new Map<string, Array<() => void>>()  
    14→// Set of currently held lock names  
    15→const held = new Set<string>()  
    16→  
    17→/**  
    18→ * Acquire a named lock. Returns a release function.  
    19→ * If the lock is already held, the caller awaits until it is released.  
    20→ */  
    21→export function acquireLock(name: string): Promise<() => void> {  
    22→  if (!held.has(name)) {  
    23→    // Lock is free — acquire immediately  
    24→    held.add(name)  
    25→    return Promise.resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    26→  }  
    27→  
    28→  // Lock is held — enqueue and wait  
    29→  return new Promise<() => void>((resolve) => {  
    30→    if (!locks.has(name)) {  
    31→      locks.set(name, [])  
    32→    }  
    33→    locks.get(name)!.push(() => {  
    34→      resolve(() => releaseLock(name))  
    35→    })  
    36→  })  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→/**  
    40→ * Release a named lock and wake the next waiter if any.  
    41→ */  
    42→function releaseLock(name: string): void {  
    43→  const queue = locks.get(name)  
    44→  if (queue && queue.length > 0) {  
    45→    // Hand lock to next waiter (don't remove from held set)  
    46→    const next = queue.shift()!  
    47→    if (queue.length === 0) {  
    48→      locks.delete(name)  
    49→    }  
    50→    next()  
    51→  } else {  
    52→    // No waiters — release the lock  
    53→    hel  

... [473 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-17 01:08:26]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Fix 2 issues in /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/hooks/useTeam.ts  

ISSUE HK-004: updateTeam optimistic update doesn't revert on network error (thrown exception). Only reverts on HTTP error (!res.ok).  

FIX: Wrap the fetch+response handling in try/catch, calling fetchTeam() in catch to revert:  
```typescript
const updateTeam = useCallback(async (updates: Partial<Team>) => {
  if (!teamId) return
  setTeam(prev => prev ? { ...prev, ...updates, updatedAt: new Date().toISOString() } : prev)
  try {
    const res = await fetch(`/api/teams/${teamId}`, {
      method: 'PUT',
      headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' },
      body: JSON.stringify(updates),
    })
    if (!res.ok) {
      await fetchTeam()  // Revert optimistic update on HTTP error
      throw new Error('Failed to update team')
    }
    const data = await res.json()
    setTeam(data.team)
  } catch (err) {
    await fetchTeam()  // Revert optimistic update on network error too
    throw err
  }
}, [teamId, fetchTeam])
```

ISSUE HK-006 (NIT): loading starts true even when teamId is null, causing a brief flash.  

FIX: Change the useState initialization from `useState(true)` to use a function initializer that checks if teamId exists. But since teamId comes from props and useState only reads the initial value, just add a comment explaining the behavior is intentional (the useEffect immediately sets loading=false when teamId is null, so the flash is a single render frame):  
```typescript
const [loading, setLoading] = useState(true)  // Set false immediately by useEffect when teamId is null
```

Read the file first. Make minimal edits.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - brief result"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator
